<p>The <b>American Red Cross</b> (<b>ARC</b>), also known as the <b>American National Red Cross</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> is a humanitarian organization that provides emergency assistance, disaster relief and education in the United States. It is the designated US affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a>.</p>
<p>The organization offers services and development programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:American_Red_Cross_headquarters.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross_National_Headquarters" title="American Red Cross National Headquarters">American Red Cross National Headquarters</a> in Washington, D.C. is a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>ARC was established in Washington, D.C. on May 21, 1881, by <a href="/wiki/Clara_Barton" title="Clara Barton">Clara Barton</a>. She became its first president. Barton organized a meeting on May 12 of that year at the home of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Omar_D._Conger" title="Omar D. Conger">Omar D. Conger</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">R</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">MI</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Fifteen people were present at this first meeting, including Barton, Conger and <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Lawrence_(Ohio_Republican)" title="William Lawrence (Ohio Republican)">William Lawrence</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">R</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">OH</a>) (who became the first vice-president<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>). The first local chapter was established in 1881 at the <a href="/wiki/English_Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Dansville" title="English Evangelical Lutheran Church of Dansville">English Evangelical Lutheran Church of Dansville</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dansville,_Livingston_County,_New_York" title="Dansville, Livingston County, New York">Dansville, New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NysNrhpNom_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-NysNrhpNom-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jane_Delano" title="Jane Delano">Jane Delano</a> (1862–1919) founded the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross_Nursing_Service" title="American Red Cross Nursing Service">American Red Cross Nursing Service</a> on January 20, 1910.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Clara_Barton">Clara Barton</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Clara Barton">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Clara_Barton" title="Clara Barton">Clara Barton</a></div>
<p>Clara Barton (1821–1912) founded the American chapter after learning of the Red Cross in Geneva, Switzerland. In 1869, she went to Europe and became involved in the work of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross" title="International Red Cross">International Red Cross</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>. She determined to bring the organization to America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clara_Barton1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="1141" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Clara_Barton1.jpg/180px-Clara_Barton1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Clara_Barton1.jpg/270px-Clara_Barton1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Clara_Barton1.jpg/360px-Clara_Barton1.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clara_Barton1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Clara_Barton" title="Clara Barton">Clara Barton</a>, founder of the American Red Cross</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Barton became President of the American branch of the society, known as the American National Red Cross in May 1881 in Washington. The first chapters opened in upstate New York, where she had connections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Ultimately, <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauri_Kovalainen" title="Lauri Kovalainen">Lars Kovala</a> and three others donated money to help create a national headquarters near the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG/220px-American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG/330px-American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG/440px-American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:American_Red_Cross_Administrative_Headquarters.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American Red Cross Administrative Headquarters in Washington, D.C.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3366" data-file-width="5112" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg/220px-USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg/330px-USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg/440px-USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USA-American_National_Red_Cross0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American National Red Cross</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Barton led one of the group's first major relief efforts, a response to the September 4–6, 1881 Great Fire of 1881 (<a href="/wiki/Thumb_Fire" title="Thumb Fire">Thumb Fire</a>) in the Thumb region of Michigan. Over 5,000 people were left homeless. The next major disaster was the <a href="/wiki/Johnstown_Flood" title="Johnstown Flood">Johnstown Flood</a>, which occurred on May 31, 1889. Over 2,209 people died and thousands more were injured in or near <a href="/wiki/Johnstown,_Pennsylvania" title="Johnstown, Pennsylvania">Johnstown, Pennsylvania</a> in one of the worst disasters in United States history.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Progressive_reform">Progressive reform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Progressive reform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Barton was unable to build up a staff she trusted and her fundraising was lackluster. She was forced out in 1904. Professional social work experts took control and made the group a model of <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Era" title="Progressive Era">Progressive Era</a> scientific reform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> New leader <a href="/wiki/Mabel_Thorp_Boardman" title="Mabel Thorp Boardman">Mabel Thorp Boardman</a> constantly consulted with senior government officials, military officers, social workers and financiers. <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> was especially influential. They imposed an ethos of "managerialism", transforming the agency from Barton's cult of personality to an "organizational humanitarianism" ready for expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ARC is a nationwide network of more than 650 chapters and 36 blood service regions. Approximately 500,000 Red Cross volunteers, including FemaCorps and <a href="/wiki/AmeriCorps" title="AmeriCorps">AmeriCorps</a> members, and 30,000 employees annually mobilize relief to people affected by more than 67,000 disasters, train almost 12 million people in necessary medical skills and exchange more than a million emergency messages for U.S. military service personnel and their family members. ARC is the largest supplier of blood and blood products to more than 3,000 hospitals and assists victims of international disasters and conflicts worldwide. In 2006 the organization had over $6 billion in total revenues. Revenue from blood and blood products alone was over $2 billion.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Recent presidents and CEOs include Gail McGovern, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Dole" title="Elizabeth Dole">Elizabeth Dole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernadine_Healy" title="Bernadine Healy">Bernadine Healy</a>, Mary S. Elcano, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_W._Everson" title="Mark W. Everson">Mark W. Everson</a> and John F. McGuire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARCLeaders_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARCLeaders-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2007, U.S. legislation clarified the role for the Board of Governors and that of the senior management in the wake of difficulties following <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking">Ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_Philanthropy" title="Chronicle of Philanthropy">Chronicle of Philanthropy</a></i>, an industry magazine, released the results of the largest study of charitable and non-profit organization popularity and credibility. The study showed that ARC was ranked as the third "most popular charity/non-profit in America" of over 100 charities researched with 48% of Americans over the age of 12 choosing "Love", and "Like A lot" to describe the Red Cross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Blood_services">Blood services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Blood services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blood_donation">Blood donation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Blood donation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ARC supplies roughly 40% of the <a href="/wiki/Blood_donation" title="Blood donation">donated blood</a> in the United States, which it sells to hospitals and regional suppliers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Community-based blood centers supply 50% and 6% is collected directly by hospitals. In December 2004, ARC completed its largest blood processing facility in the United States in <a href="/wiki/Pomona,_California" title="Pomona, California">Pomona, California</a>, on the campus grounds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cal_Poly_Pomona" title="Cal Poly Pomona">California State Polytechnic University, Pomona</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tissue_services">Tissue services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tissue services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For more than 50 years, ARC provided <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allograft" title="Allograft">allograft</a> tissue for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" title="Organ transplant">transplant</a> through sales in its Tissue Services Program. It cared for thousands of donor families who gave the gift of tissue donation and sold donated tissue to more than 1 million transplant recipients in need of this life saving or life-enhancing gift of tissue. At the end of January 2005, ARC ended its Tissue Services program in order to focus on its primary missions of Disaster Relief and Blood Services.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plasma_services">Plasma services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Plasma services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A leader in the <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma" title="Blood plasma">plasma</a> industry, ARC provides more than one quarter of the nation's plasma products. Red Cross Plasma Services provides plasma products that are reliable, cost-effective and as safe as possible.</p>
<p>In February 1999, ARC completed its "Transformation", a $287 million program that: re-engineered Red Cross Blood Services' processing, testing and distribution system; and established a new management structure.</p>
<p>As of 2011, ARC was no longer in the Plasma Services industry. The Red Cross supplies <a href="/wiki/Baxter_International" title="Baxter International">Baxter BioSciences</a> with items for the manufacturing of plasma products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nucleic_acid_testing">Nucleic acid testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Nucleic acid testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 1, 1999, ARC became the first U.S. blood bank to implement a <a href="/wiki/Nucleic_acid_test" title="Nucleic acid test">Nucleic acid testing</a> (NAT) study. This process is different from traditional testing because it looks for the <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetic</a> material of HIV and <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">hepatitis C</a> (HCV), rather than the body's response to the disease.</p>
<p>The NAT tests for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RT-PCR_test" title="RT-PCR test">HIV</a> and HCV have been licensed by the U.S.<a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA). These tests detect the genetic material of a transfusion-transmitted virus like HIV without waiting for the body to form antibodies, potentially offering an important time advantage over current techniques.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leukoreduction">Leukoreduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Leukoreduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leukocytes" title="Leukocytes">Leukocytes</a> (white blood cells) help fight off foreign substances such as bacteria, viruses and abnormal cells. In fact, these foreign leukocytes in transfused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_blood_cells" title="Red blood cells">red blood cells</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platelets" title="Platelets">platelets</a> are often not well tolerated and have been associated with some types of transfusion complications. Leukocytes in stored blood products can have a variety of biological effects, including depression of immune function, which can result in organ failure and death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Because whole blood is rarely used for transfusion and not kept in routine inventory, leukoreduced red blood supplies are critical. After collection the whole blood is separated into red cells and plasma by centrifugation. A preservative solution is mixed with the red cells and the component is filtered with a leukoreduction filter. Shelf life for this product is 42 days.</p>
<p>ARC is moving toward system-wide universal prestorage leukocyte reduction to improve patient care. From 1976 through 1985, the FDA received reports of 355 fatalities associated with transfusion, 99 of which were excluded from further review because they were unrelated to transfusion or involved <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">hepatitis</a> or <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">acquired immune deficiency syndrome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> While the FDA has not yet made a leukoreduction a requirement, ARC took a leading role in implementing this procedure with a goal of leukoreducing all blood products. More than 70 percent of ARC red blood cell components undergo prestorage leukoreduction, a filtering process that is done soon after blood is donated.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ARC operates the <a href="/wiki/Jerome_H._Holland" title="Jerome H. Holland">Jerome H. Holland</a> blood laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Rockville,_Maryland" title="Rockville, Maryland">Rockville, Maryland</a>. Each year,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the Red Cross invests more than $25 million in research activities at the Holland Laboratory and in the field.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cellular_therapies">Cellular therapies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cellular therapies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ARC offers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_therapy" title="Cellular therapy">cellular therapies</a>; this treatment involves collecting and treating blood cells from a patient or other blood donor. The treated cells are then introduced into a patient to help revive normal cell function, replace cells that are lost as a result of disease, accidents or aging, or to prevent illnesses from appearing.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_safety_services">Health and safety services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health and safety services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>ARC provides <a href="/wiki/First_aid" title="First aid">first aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation" title="Cardiopulmonary resuscitation">cardiopulmonary resuscitation</a> (CPR), <a href="/wiki/Automated_external_defibrillator" title="Automated external defibrillator">automated external defibrillator</a> (AED), water safety and <a href="/wiki/Lifeguard" title="Lifeguard">lifeguarding</a>, babysitting, disaster preparedness and home safety training throughout the United States. Training programs are primarily aimed at laypersons, workplaces and aquatic facilities<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. ARC teaches around 12 million Americans these skills annually, ranging from youth to professional rescuers. ARC co-led the 2005 Guidelines for First Aid, which aims to provide up-to-date and peer-reviewed first aid training materials. Many American Red Cross chapters also have for sale first aid kits, disaster kits, and similar, related equipment. Many chapters of ARC offer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pet_first_aid_courses" title="Pet first aid courses">pet first aid courses</a> to prepare pet owners and pet professionals for emergency situations. ARC also offers a pet first aid reference guide. This guide includes a 50-minute DVD that informs viewers about safety procedures and instructs on dealing with medical emergencies.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disaster_services">Disaster services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Disaster services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_2332_-_Photograph_by_Robert_A._Eplett_taken_on_01-17-1994_in_California.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
